## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration (dv_dt) is governed by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). Nonlinearities appear as higher-order terms in x and v.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol form 2: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (harmonic external driving)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (general nonlinear driven oscillator)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * v**2) (velocity-dependent friction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x²) break symmetry and introduce DC offset in oscillations
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type self-excited oscillations
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces or parametric excitation
- The sign of the cubic term x³ determines hardening (same sign as linear term) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v³) represent dissipative forces; negative linear v coefficient with positive x²*v creates limit cycle behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or exchanged through position/velocity-dependent mechanisms
- Products of x and trigonometric functions of t suggest parametric resonance phenomena where the natural frequency is modulated
- Multiple competing nonlinear terms (e.g., -v + x²*v) can create bifurcations between stable equilibrium and limit cycle oscillations
